These well-maintained rate profiles further corroborate the robust performance that can be attributed to the enhanced interphase.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0021_R_d61446837e1543" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Indeed, the improved low-temperature performance of NPDDF is largely due to the increased ionic diffusion resulting from the abundant NaF and polar O = C-O-R and -OSO<sub>2</sub>- species in the CEI layer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0023_R_d61446837e1551" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202415680-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f191da19-02fd-4875-8fe7-495c1b81611a/adfm202415680-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f191da19-02fd-4875-8fe7-495c1b81611a/adfm202415680-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/eaa7f615-3b82-4bbb-bf60-a80e0a374486/adfm202415680-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f191da19-02fd-4875-8fe7-495c1b81611a/adfm202415680-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202415680-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202415680" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical performance of NVP within NPF and NPDDF at −25 °C: a) cycling at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>; b) rate capabilities and c) rate profiles; d) long-term cycling at 20.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>; e) cycling performance of full cell based on NVP/HC at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Electrochemical performance of NVP within NPF and NPDDF at 60 °C: f) cycling at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>; g) rate capabilities and h) rate profiles; i) long-term cycling at 20.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>; j) cycling performance of full cell based on NVP/HC at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>Beyond low-temperature performance, the electrochemical behavior at 60 °C further validates the enhanced interphase integrity provided by the NPDDF electrolyte. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202415680-fig-0006">6f</a>, NVP in NPDDF achieves a high capacity of 112.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, nearly reaching its theoretical limit. This can be attributed to the improved ionic kinetics and the stability of the interphase at elevated temperatures.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0025_R_d61446837e1597" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Although both electrolytes exhibit some degree of voltage polarization (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202415680-fig-0006">6g</a>), NPDDF significantly outperforms NPF in rate capability, with a capacity of 70.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 40.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, whereas NPF shows almost no capacity (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202415680-fig-0006">6h</a>). This superior performance of NPDDF continues even at a higher current density of 20.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202415680-fig-0006">6i</a>), with reversible capacities of 79.6 (NPDDF) and 64.1 (NPF) mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 3000 cycles, respectively, indicating a stable interphase with high-temperature tolerance. It should be noted that the specific capacities of NVP within NPDDF and NPF during long-term cycling exceed those observed in rate tests at 60 °C. In general, the fluctuations in current density during rate test cause variations in electrochemical polarization, leading to nonuniform current distribution, electrode structure damage, and interphase degradation, all of which detrimentally affect the specific capacity output.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0008_R_d61446837e1621" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Adv. Energy Mater.">8</a>, <a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0017_R_d61446837e1621" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">17</a>, <a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0065_R_d61446837e1621" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - Battery Energy">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To further clarify our test results, we repeated the long-term cycling test at 20.0 A g<sup>−1</sup> at 60 °C for NVP electrode within the NPDDF. The results, as depicted in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S23</a> (Supporting Information), show an initial specific capacity of 89.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> and an average capacity of 77.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 3000 cycles. These results are close to our previous data, confirming reliability of our electrochemical test results. As shown in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information), the NVP electrodes within the NPDDF exhibit outstanding electrochemical performance over a broad temperature ranging from −25 to 60 °C, validating the effectiveness of our electrolyte design. Moreover, Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a> (Supporting Information) presents a comparison of the electrochemical performance of NVP-based electrodes across wide temperature, from where it is believed that the excellent compatibility of NVP with the specifically designed NPDDF results in comparable electrochemical performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0017_R_d61446837e1642" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">17</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Beyond the comparison of specific capacity and cycling stability across temperatures from −25 to 60 °C between NPDDF and NPF, the comparison of Coulombic efficiency (CE) shown in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> (Supporting Information) indicates that both the first and hundredth cycles for the NVP electrodes in both electrolytes exhibit consistently high CEs, demonstrating excellent electrochemical reversibility.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0039_R_d61446837e1651" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Energy Mater.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For the full cell, the NVP coupled with HC in NPDDF demonstrates a reversible capacity of 74.9 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles at 0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, achieving ≈100% CE (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202415680-fig-0006">6j</a>). Noting that the full cell performance at 60 °C is inferior to that at 25 °C, and this decline in performance should be primarily due to increased temperature elevating the rate of undesirable side reactions, which stem from the degradation of the electrolyte and the destabilization of the electrode/electrolyte interphase.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0007_R_d61446837e1663" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Chem. Sci.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Besides, our analysis for the interfacial charge transfer through EIS reveals that the interfacial charge transfer at 60 °C is inferior compared with that at 25 °C upon cycling (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a>, Supporting Information), providing evidence for their discrepancy on electrochemical performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0039_R_d61446837e1672" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Energy Mater.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Furthermore, rate tests (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a>, Supporting Information) reveal that the full cell maintains a high capacity of 62.0 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 2.0 A g<sup>−1</sup>, which underscores its robust electrochemical performance even at high current densities. The primary cause of performance degradation at high temperatures is typically interphase degradation; however, the inclusion of -OSO<sub>2</sub>- species and NaF in the CEI significantly enhances its integrity, thus contributing to the stable electrochemical performance observed at 60 °C.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0014_R_d61446837e1687" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Energy Environ. Sci.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>The above electrochemical performances of NVP in NPDDF have evidently revealed the excellent compatibility between the NVP electrode and NPDDF electrolyte as well as the stability of the generated interphase. To further evaluate the stability of the modified interphase formed in NPDDF, the assessing of charge transfer upon cycling, interphase component variations, and interphase morphology were performed. As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S24</a> (Supporting Information), the EIS of NVP electrode within NPDDF upon cycling at 25 °C show the almost overlapped semi-circles in middle frequency region, corresponding to charge transfer resistance, at selected cycles, indicating rapid interfacial charge transfer and generation of stable interphase.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0004_R_d61446837e1697" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Energy Environ. Sci.">4</a>, <a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0039" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0039_R_d61446837e1697" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 39 - Adv. Energy Mater.">39</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> For the EIS at −25 and 60 °C, although the plots collected at selected cycles exhibit inferior on stability over those at 25 °C, the slight variations on the semi-circles are acceptable, especially considering the low (−25 °C) and high (60 °C) operation temperatures, which reveals the good stability of the interphase.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0055_R_d61446837e1702" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Energy Storage Mater.">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Turning to interphase components, analyses of deconvoluted spectra of C 1s, F 1s, Na 1s, O 1s, and S 2p for the NVP electrode within NPDDF after 10 and 100 cycles show minimal variations on the interphase components (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26</a>, Supporting Information). Both peak intensity and positions maintain well, thus clearly indicating the interphase's structural integrity and stability under repeated cycling conditions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0035_R_d61446837e1711" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Adv. Mater.">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Lastly, recognizing that interphase degradation is the main factor behind battery performance deterioration at high temperatures, we conducted high-resolution transmission microscope （HRTEM） to assess interphase stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0007_R_d61446837e1716" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Chem. Sci.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a> (Supporting Information), HRTEM images of the NVP electrode after 100 cycles at 60 °C (0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>) reveal that continuous electrolyte decomposition in NPF leads to the formation of a thick and coarse CEI layer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0047_R_d61446837e1727" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast, the NPDDF electrolyte results in a more uniform and smoother CEI layer. This significant difference can be attributed to the preferential decomposition of the coordinated structures containing DMS and DES in NPDDF, which forms a CEI layer enriched with sulfur and fluorine species.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0012_R_d61446837e1732" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Adv. Sci.">12</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> These sulfur species, together with inorganic NaF, play a crucial role in maintaining the integrity of the interphase.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0023_R_d61446837e1738" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, a comparison of the SEI layers on the HC electrode (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a>, Supporting Information) further illustrates the disparity between the two electrolytes. After cycling, the interphase formed in NPDDF is noticeably more uniform than that in NPF. Additionally, the thinner SEI layer observed in NPDDF, compared to the thicker SEI layer in NPF, reinforces the superior interphase integrity provided by the sulfur and fluorine species. This enhanced interphase not only supports better electrochemical performance but also ensures greater durability and stability, especially under extreme temperature conditions.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202415680-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202415680-bib-0029_R_d61446837e1746" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Energy Environ. Sci.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202415680-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202415680-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In this work, we have successfully addressed the challenges of sluggish ionic migration at low temperatures and interphase instability at high temperatures in SIBs by proposing a sulfur-rich interphase enhancement strategy. By implementing this approach, we have developed modified CEI/SEI layers that exhibit both improved ionic kinetics and superior structural integrity. Consequently, these modifications enable exceptional performance of SIBs within a carbonate-based electrolyte across an extended temperature range from −25 to 60 °C. Crucially, the involvement of DMS and DES in the coordinated structure within the NPDDF electrolyte plays a pivotal role in this enhancement. Specifically, their inclusion promotes the formation of -OSO<sub>2</sub>- species in the CEI layer, which, when working in synergy with NaF, ensures not only efficient ionic migration but also robust interphase integrity. As a result, the full cells based on NVP and HC, which exhibit reversible capacities of 80.7, 56.0, and 74.8 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, corresponding to capacity retentions of 97.7%, 87.6%, and 88.3% at 25, −25, and 60 °C, respectively. These impressive results underscore the effectiveness of our electrolyte modification in enhancing battery performance under extreme temperature conditions. Furthermore, the detailed molecular dynamics simulations and dynamic tests conducted in this study provide additional confirmation of the superiority of the CEI layer modified with sulfur species.</p>
         </section>
